            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402178-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/06e1493d-94c7-488a-b8e3-87f9f7b0a7da/adfm202402178-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/06e1493d-94c7-488a-b8e3-87f9f7b0a7da/adfm202402178-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/02c4eb9b-d559-4af1-95a4-6d721ee28423/adfm202402178-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/06e1493d-94c7-488a-b8e3-87f9f7b0a7da/adfm202402178-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402178-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402178" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Structural evolution of SCMX6 electrode during sodium storage. a) TEM images of pristine and after cycles SCMX6, scale bar: 50&nbsp;nm a,b); 2&nbsp;nm (inset of b). c) Schematic of the formation process of Cu<sub>2</sub>S NPs in SCMX6 under electrochemical driving force. d) Charge/discharge curves of SCMX6 and corresponding in-situ XRD contour pattern. Ex-situ XRD patterns of SCMX6 electrode during e) the 1st and f) the 3rd discharge/charge processes. HRTEM and TEM mapping images of SCMX6 electrode at different states for the 1st cycle: g,h) discharge to 0.01&nbsp;V, scale bars: 2&nbsp;nm g) and 50&nbsp;nm h); i,j) charge to 3.0&nbsp;V, scale bars: 2&nbsp;nm i) and 50&nbsp;nm j). l,m) Ex situ XPS. l) Cu 2p, and m) Auger Cu LMM spectra of SCMX6 electrode after 100 cycles.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The elemental species and valence states of SCMX6 after fully cycling were further investigated by ex situ XPS. The peaks in the Cu 2<i>p</i> spectrum at 932.6 and 952.3&nbsp;eV can be attributed to Cu<sup>+</sup>, and the peaks at 933.8 and 953.7&nbsp;eV can be attributed to Cu<sup>2+</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0003">3k</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0035_R_d216912174e1277" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Energy Stor. Mater.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the Cu LMM Auger spectrum at 917 and 921&nbsp;eV showed two peaks corresponding to Cu(I) and Cu(0), respectively, confirming that Cu(I) is predominantly present (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0003">3l</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0033_R_d216912174e1286" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Energy Stor. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The S 2<i>p</i> spectrum of the cycled SCMX6 electrode was divided into five peaks (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information), of which the two peaks located at 161.8 and 162.9&nbsp;eV can be attributed to Cu<sub>2</sub>S, whereas the peaks at 163.7 and 165.0&nbsp;eV are C−S−C bond, and the peak at 168.9&nbsp;eV is attributed to the oxidized S species.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0033_R_d216912174e1299" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Energy Stor. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This further demonstrates the in-situ formation of Cu<sub>2</sub>S, while the carbon still has the S component in the doped state, which is conducive to enhancing the adsorption capacity of the carbon matrix. In addition, we analyzed the S content in SCMX6 (24.929&nbsp;wt.%, Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information), which is ≈62.25% of the mass of the actual active material after it is fully converted to Cu<sub>2</sub>S (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information). This strategy of in situ introducing Cu<sub>2</sub>S NPs during the cycling process greatly increased the number of active sites without damaging the function of the Cu current collector, which is favorable for the sodium storage performance.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202402178-sec-0060-title">2.4 Electrochemical Sodium Storage Performance</h3>
            
            <p>In order to explore the electrochemical behavior of SCMX electrodes during charging and discharging, CV curves were tested. In the first cycle of SCMX6 (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4a</a>), the reduction peaks at 1.80 and 1.12&nbsp;V can be attributed to the multi-step conversion reaction of S originating in the carbon matrix with Na<sup>+</sup>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0036_R_d216912174e1334" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Energy Environ. Sci.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> but gradually disappear in subsequent cycles, which is related to the in situ formation of Cu<sub>2</sub>S.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0037_R_d216912174e1342" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Energy Stor. Mater.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The reduction peak located at 0.12&nbsp;V, which does not exist in the following cycles, is ascribed to the irreversible decomposition of electrolytes and the formation of SEI films.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0026_R_d216912174e1347" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Energy Stor. Mater. Adv. Mater.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The anodic peaks at 1.80, 1.85, and 2.13&nbsp;V correspond to the gradual conversion of Na<sub>2</sub>S to Na<sup>+</sup>. In the subsequent cycles, cathodic peaks at 1.96&nbsp;V correspond to the formation of Cu<sup>+</sup>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0033_R_d216912174e1359" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Energy Stor. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and 1.5 and 0.83&nbsp;V correspond to the multi-step conversion reaction of Cu<sub>2</sub>S with Na<sup>+</sup> and the formation of Na<sub>y</sub>Cu<sub>x</sub>S.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0038_R_d216912174e1373" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Adv. Energy Mater. Matter">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Afterward, Na<sub>y</sub>Cu<sub>x</sub>S undergoes a conversion reaction and decomposes to Na<sub>2</sub>S and Cu, corresponding to a cathodic peak of 0.40&nbsp;V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0039_R_d216912174e1385" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nat. Commun.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the anodic scan, the two peaks at 1.55 and 2.13&nbsp;V correspond to the conversion from Cu and Na<sub>2</sub>S to Na<sub>y</sub>Cu<sub>x</sub>S and the deintercalation from Na<sub>y</sub>Cu<sub>x</sub>S to Cu<sub>2</sub>S, respectively. The CV curves of the first three cycles exhibited less consistent shapes, suggesting that the electrode undergoes irreversible S-species transformations (from C−S to Cu−S bonds) at the initial stage, which is also observed in SC and other SCMXs electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information). After several cycles, the dQ/dV curves of the 5–9th cycles remained almost identical (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that the active material in the electrode had almost ceased to change at this point and had become well reversible.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402178-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6b055056-bf70-484d-9c3c-1fe57d7a7b10/adfm202402178-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/6b055056-bf70-484d-9c3c-1fe57d7a7b10/adfm202402178-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c850ac16-c926-45c7-add7-6681d930137d/adfm202402178-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6b055056-bf70-484d-9c3c-1fe57d7a7b10/adfm202402178-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402178-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402178" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Sodium-ion storage performance. a) CV curves of SCMX6 at 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. b) Cycling performance at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. c) ICE and reversible capacity at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 150 cycles of SCMX6 versus other reported state-of-the-art HC-based anodes (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). d) Rate performance. e) Profiles of charge/discharge at various current densities for SCMX6. f) Rate capacity retention comparison of SCMX6 with advanced anode materials (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). g) Long-term cycling stability at a high current density of 50&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after an initial 3 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Inset depicts the charge/discharge profile of the SCMX6 electrode at 4502–4510 cycles, demonstrating that SCMX6 achieves complete charging within a remarkably short duration of 24&nbsp;s.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Sodium storage performance enhancement relying on the dual-biomimetic architecture was verified by systematic electrochemical characterization. SCMX6 exhibits the highest specific capacity compared to other electrodes, which is related to its abundant accessible active sites, rich heterogeneous interfaces, and good electrode-electrolyte contact (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4b</a>). After 150 cycles at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the reversible capacity of SCMX6 gradually increased to 745.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> due to the continuous electrolyte penetration, in-situ formed Cu<sub>2</sub>S, and successful activation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0040_R_d216912174e1458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - ACS Mater. Lett.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> SCMX6 electrode simultaneously exhibits an impressive ICE of 95.2% and a remarkable reversible capacity, both of which can be attributed to the robust structural stability of the SCMX6 electrode and its highly reversible sodium-ion storage behavior (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4c</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Most importantly, SCMX6 electrode exhibits excellent rate performance—a high specific capacity of 380.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at an ultrahigh current density of 50&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, much higher than those of SC (176.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), SCMX3 (266.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and SCMX12 (212.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4d</a>). When the current density is reduced to 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, SCMX6 exhibits a high capacity of ≈667.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is related to the gradual penetration of the electrolyte and the in-situ formation of Cu<sub>2</sub>S providing additional active sites. The results show the advantages of the dual-biomimetic gradient hierarchical architecture in excellent structure stability and ultrahigh-rate capability. The charge/discharge curves of electrode SCMX6 at various current densities (from 0.1 to 50&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) show a similar shape (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4e</a>), demonstrating the sodium storage behavior is well maintained in a wide range of operating currents. Meanwhile, the SCMX6 electrode exhibits an exceptional capacity retention in high rates for SIBs that far surpasses the best results of the advanced anodes reported up to date, especially at 50&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (capacity retention of 64.4% compared to 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4f</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Although the in-situ generation of Cu<sub>2</sub>S NPs is conducive to the enhancement of sodium storage performance, the lack of a rational spatial architecture still makes it difficult to fulfill its role. To evaluate the cycling stability of the electrodes at ultrahigh current densities, a long-term cycling test of 50&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> was performed on SC and SCMXs after 3 cycles of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> activation (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4g</a>). The SCMX6 electrode maintained an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 337.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 5000 cycles (≈100% capacity retention compared to the 4th cycle). The enlarged charge/discharge curve of the SCMX6 electrode at cycles of 4502–4510 (inset in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0004">4g</a>) showed that the curve shapes are consistent, and a charging duration is only 24&nbsp;s, thus exhibiting commendable cycling stability and exceptionally rapid charging rate. Meanwhile, SC electrode has obvious deficiencies in long-life cycling compared to SCMXs electrodes, which is related to the fact that SC random stacking does not form a stable spatial architecture. The SCMX6 exhibits exceptional stability with a capacity of 287.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> even after undergoing 10&nbsp;000 cycles at an ultrahigh current density of 80&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>; the results further indicate the robustness of its dual bionic structure (capacity retention of 98.2%) and show the outstanding performance compared to those of the reported anode materials for SIBs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0001">1d</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). The average capacity decay per cycle is only 0.00018% and the Coulombic efficiency remains ≈100% throughout the cycles, indicating its excellent structural stability under the ultralong cycling test.</p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">CV tests were examined at various scan rates to further explore the rapid sodium storage kinetics of SCMX6 electrodes. The CV curves in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5a</a> exhibit similar profiles with reduced peak separation, indicating diminished polarization at higher rates. The measured peak currents (<i>i</i>) and scan rates (<i>v</i>) are related by the following equation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0041_R_d216912174e1550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Phys. Chem. B">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202402178-disp-0004"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/1d958833-7621-4e73-bc6c-43444eeafd19/adfm202402178-math-0004.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202402178:adfm202402178-math-0004" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202402178-math-0004.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>i</mi>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                              <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                              <mi>a</mi>
                              <msup>
                                 <mi>v</mi>
                                 <mi>b</mi>
                              </msup>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}i\ = \ a{{v}^b}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>where <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are constants. The <i>b</i>-value is correlated with the kinetic behavior of the material. <i>b</i>-values of 0.5 and 1 indicate that the electrode materials are dominated by a diffusion-dominated cell behavior and a surface-induced pseudocapacitance contribution, respectively. SCMX6 exhibits the highest <i>b</i>-values (0.91–0.98) at different redox peak positions, indicating a surface-induced pseudocapacitive process (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5b</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information). SCMX6 electrode also exhibited a significantly higher capacitive contribution of 99% at 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5c</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information) compared to other electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22–S24</a>, Supporting Information). The results show that the high capacitance contribution of SCMX6 stems from: 1) a continuous conductive network that enables the rapid transfer of electrons; 2) a unique dual biomimetic architecture as well as in situ formation of Cu<sub>2</sub>S NPs, which allows for rapid redox reactions at or near the surface; 3) a large specific surface area and many mesopores, which provide a channel for the rapid transport of sodium ions. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5d</a>, the EIS tests were employed to further study the charge transfer kinetics of all electrodes. All the Nyquist plots show 1) a semicircle in the high-frequency region, representing the resistance of charge transfer between the electrode materials and electrolyte (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>); and 2) a sloping line in the low-frequency region, standing for Warburg impedance related to Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the solid phase (<i>Z</i><sub>w</sub>). The SCMX6 electrode displays the smallest <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (1.31&nbsp;Ω) than that of SC (15.27&nbsp;Ω), SCMX3 (3.82&nbsp;Ω), and SCMX12 (22.4&nbsp;Ω), indicating a fast charge transfer process. In addition, the minimum Warburg impedance coefficient (σ) indicates that SCMX6 has a more rapid Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics due to the gradient hierarchical architecture and its rich surface and interface (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5e</a>, the calculation formula is detailed in the Supporting information). To gain a more comprehensive understanding of the rapid reaction kinetics, we conducted an XPS analysis on the composition of its SEI layer after 3 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting information). Both SC and SCMX6 were found to form organic-inorganic hybridized SEI layers; the SEI layer of SCMX6 was thinner and had a higher NaF content, which was favorable for rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transport. To further study the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics of the electrodes, all materials were tested and analyzed using galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5f</a>. SCMX6 anode exhibits a bigger sodium ion diffusion coefficient (<span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/3f6ae6cc-3ed3-4fb5-a8fe-132d0a0e590d/adfm202402178-math-0005.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202402178:adfm202402178-math-0005" display="inline" location="graphic/adfm202402178-math-0005.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>a</mi>
                              <mo>+</mo>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                     </msub>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{N{{a}^ + }}}$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math>) than others. The enhanced <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/271a8074-aefa-40b9-a5dd-2df59d695079/adfm202402178-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202402178:adfm202402178-math-0006" display="inline" location="graphic/adfm202402178-math-0006.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>a</mi>
                              <mo>+</mo>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                     </msub>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{N{{a}^ + }}}$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> related to its unique architecture, including 1) the coral polyp-like structure provides more electrode/electrolyte interface for sufficient charge transfer reaction; 2) in-situ formed Cu<sub>2</sub>S NPs&nbsp;and abundant defects provide highly accessible active sites for fast sodium storage; 3) a large number of carbon/Cu<sub>2</sub>S and carbon/MXene heterogeneous interfaces effectively reduces the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barrier; 4) the thinner and NaF-rich SEI layer favors for rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transport.</div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402178-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4e21f795-754f-4d74-86d9-f08adcec3d54/adfm202402178-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4e21f795-754f-4d74-86d9-f08adcec3d54/adfm202402178-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3ecf6ff6-ae68-4131-9ff5-96765b2537bd/adfm202402178-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4e21f795-754f-4d74-86d9-f08adcec3d54/adfm202402178-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402178-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402178" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Sodium storage kinetics analysis. a) CV curves of SCMX6 under various scan rates. b) Log (peak current) versus log (scan rate) plots at different redox peaks of SCMX6. c) Normalized contribution ratio at different scan rates. d) Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) data. e) Linear fits of the Z’ versus ω<sup>−1/2</sup> in the low-frequency region (slope is the Warburg impedance coefficient). f) GITT curves and the corresponding Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/8a3410c0-1c57-4dd7-96c2-1f34545f3546/adfm202402178-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202402178:adfm202402178-math-0007" display="inline" location="graphic/adfm202402178-math-0007.png">
                           <semantics>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi>D</mi>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                                    <msup>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                                       <mo>+</mo>
                                    </msup>
                                 </mrow>
                              </msub>
                              <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}}$</annotation>
                           </semantics></math>) of different electrodes. g) Schematic illustrating the sodium storage mechanism of dual-biomimetic gradient hierarchical architecture SCMX6: highly accessible active sites on the surface induce fast pseudocapacitance-dominated kinetics; MCCHS/MXene heterogeneous interface and MXene accelerate ion/electron transport; flex-rigid spine-like structure, as well as concave and porous carbon mitigate volume expansion step by step to enhance stability and durability.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The aforementioned electrochemical test and structural characterization indicated that the fast sodium storage behavior and exceptional sodium storage performance of the SCMX6 electrode can be attributed to several factors (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0005">5g</a>): 1) The distinctive biomimetic coral polyp design facilitates electrolyte and ion accessibility, and the abundant redox sites (both C−S bonds and Cu<sub>2</sub>S NPs) on anode surface enhance pseudocapacitive-dominated kinetics. 2) MXene and the chemically jointed heterogeneous interface of MCCHS/MXene construct rapid electron transfer and transportation pathways. 3) The flex-rigid spine-like structure as well as mesoporous concave carbon for SCMX6 mitigate volume expansion during sodiation step by step to enhance mechanical stability and durability.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202402178-sec-0070-title">2.5 Full-Cell Electrochemical Performance Characterization</h3>
            
            <p>To further show the exceptional performance and the practical expansibility of SCMX6, high-power full cells were demonstrated by taking SICs as an example (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6a</a>). Generally speaking, the kinetic mismatch between the battery-type anode and the capacitive-type cathode poses a challenge for the practical application of SICs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0042_R_d216912174e1731" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The dual-biomimetic SCMX6 anode, characterized by high pseudocapacitance contribution for fast sodium ion storage, can bridge the kinetic gap mentioned above and bring excellent long-cycling stability when combined with an activated carbon (AC) cathode (Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information). To achieve optimal electrode capacity matching, the anode and cathode are optimized in a 1:1 mass ratio (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information). Both the CV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6b</a>) and galvanostatic charge-discharge&nbsp;(Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6c</a>) curves of the SICs full-cell deviate slightly from the ideal rectangular and linear slope, mainly due to a hybrid energy storage mechanism in the anode and cathode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0043_R_d216912174e1752" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Energy Environ. Sci.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The SCMX6//AC SICs exhibited excellent rate performance (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information), maintaining a high capacity retention of 71.7% (compared to 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) at current densities up to 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The maximum energy density of SICs reaches up to 78.1&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at 400.7&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>; 50.68&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> can be retained even at a high power output of 35&nbsp;878&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the sum of anode and cathode active mass). The Ragone plot (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6d</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information) demonstrates that the SCMX6//AC SICs exhibit a high power density, surpassing advanced SICs. More interestingly, at a high current density of 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity retention of SCMX6//AC SICs after 10&nbsp;000 ultralong cycles was 93.3%, corresponding to a capacity loss of only 0.00068% per cycle (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6e</a>). Moreover, the cycling stability of SCMX6/AC SICs at high current density surpasses all reported advanced SICs, demonstrating its superior durability (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). The high capacity retention and fast charging/discharging capability at high current densities are attributed to the structural stability and the pseudocapacitive-dominated fast sodium storage behavior of SCMX6. The coin-type SICs can effectively power a small wind-powered aircraft and a hygrothermograph as well as illuminate the “SIFE” sign consisting of 58 light-emitting diodes (LEDs) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6f,g</a>; Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a>, Supporting Information) to demonstrate our concept. The above tests show that the SCMX6//AC SICs hold promise in high-power applications in the future, such as wearable IoT devices, public transportation, power storage stations, and forklift trucks (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402178-fig-0006">6h</a>).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402178-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/509abb49-7be0-4a62-8784-41c9f09267b6/adfm202402178-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/509abb49-7be0-4a62-8784-41c9f09267b6/adfm202402178-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6b41d005-5fcb-4cca-9bcd-3710f46de4bc/adfm202402178-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/509abb49-7be0-4a62-8784-41c9f09267b6/adfm202402178-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402178-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402178" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance and application of SCMX6/AC SICs. a) Schematic of the SCMX6/AC SICs. b) CV curves at various scan rates. c) Charge/discharge curves at different current densities. d) Ragone plots of SCMX6/AC SICs compared with reported advanced SICs. e) Long-term cycling performance of SCMX6/AC SICs at a high current density of 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (after initial 3 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Inset depicts the charge/discharge profile of the SICs at 9000–9010th cycles, demonstrating the ability to complete a full charge/discharge cycle within 17.6&nbsp;s. f) Photos of SCMX6/AC SICs powering micro-engine airplanes. g) Photos of SCMX6/AC SICs illuminating the “SIFE” logo consisting of 58 LEDs in the light and dark. h) Application prospects for SICs include wearable IoT devices, public transportation, power storage stations, high-power devices for factories, etc.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202402178-sec-0080-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we developed a novel and facile strategy to fabricate dual-biomimetic gradient hierarchical architecture by controllable physical electrostatic-induced co-assembly and chemical heterogeneous bonding. The architecture enjoys high ion/electrolyte accessibility, fast ion storage and conversion capabilities, rapid ion/electron transport pathways, and excellent mechanical stability and flexibility. As a consequence, sodium-ion storage performance at ultrahigh-rate is effectively improved, maintaining a high reversible capacity of 287.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 80&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 10&nbsp;000 cycles (the average capacity decay per cycle is only 0.00018%). The surface capacitance-controlled sodium storage kinetics effectively bridges the gap with the kinetics of AC cathode, thereby yielding excellent electrochemical performance of the assembled SICs (including high power density of 35&nbsp;878&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, and high capacity retention of 93.3% after 10&nbsp;000 cycles at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). The work may provide inspiration for structural design and a promising avenue for the future application of high-rate energy storage systems.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0090">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202402178-sec-0090-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0100">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0110">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402178-sec-0120-title"> Materials</h4>
                  
                  <p>Tetraethyl orthosilicate (&gt;99%), resorcinol (AR), formaldehyde solution (ACS, 37&nbsp;wt.% in water), ammonia solution (AR, 25–28%), N-methylpyrrolidone (99.5%), and LiCl (AR) were purchased from Aladdin. HCl acid (AR, 36%–38%), sulfur powder (99.9%), and absolute ethanol (99.9%) were purchased from Sinopharm Chemical Reagent Co., Ltd. HF acid (40%, Xilong Scientific Co., Ltd.), Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> MAX (400 mesh, Foshan Xinxi Technology Co., Ltd.), ketjen black (ECP600JD, Lion Co.), carboxymethylcellulose sodium (Daicel Co.), polyvinylidene fluoride (HSV 900, Arkema), carbon nanotubes (Nanjing XFNANO Materials Tech Co., Ltd.), AC (YP-80F, Kuraray China Co., Ltd.). All materials were used as received.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402178-sec-0130-title"> Preparation of MCCHS</h4>
                  
                  <p>Typically, 13.84&nbsp;mL of tetraethyl orthosilicate was added to a mixture of 280&nbsp;mL of absolute ethanol, 12&nbsp;mL of ammonia solution, and 40&nbsp;mL of deionized (DI) water, and then stirred vigorously for 15&nbsp;min at 25&nbsp;°C. 1.6&nbsp;g of resorcinol and 2.24&nbsp;mL of formaldehyde solution were added to the above solution and stirred for 24&nbsp;h. The precipitate obtained by centrifugation with DI water and absolute ethanol several times was placed in a tube furnace and carbonized at 700&nbsp;°C with a heating rate of 5&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> under Ar atmosphere for 2&nbsp;h. Finally, the SiO<sub>2</sub> template was removed with HF acid to obtain MCCHS.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402178-sec-0140-title"> Preparation of Single or Few-Layered Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub> MXene Nanosheets Suspension</h4>
                  
                  <p>Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub> MXene suspensions were obtained using a modified liquid-phase etching strategy of Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> MAX powder.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402178-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402178-bib-0044_R_d216912174e1904" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Nature">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Typically, 1&nbsp;g of Ti<sub>3</sub>AlC<sub>2</sub> powder was slowly added to a polytetrafluoroethylene beaker containing a mixture of 18&nbsp;mL of 9&nbsp;M HCl and 2&nbsp;mL of 40% HF acid, then stirred at 35&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h. Next, the solution was washed and centrifuged with DI water until the supernatant reached a pH value of 6. The precipitate was added to 50&nbsp;mL of DI water containing 1&nbsp;g LiCl and stirred for 18&nbsp;h. After washing away the residual LiCl with DI water, the precipitate was mixed with ≈50&nbsp;mL DI water and bath sonicated (&lt;5&nbsp;°C to avoid possible oxidation) for 1&nbsp;h under the protection of Ar atmosphere. Finally, the mixture was centrifuged at 3500&nbsp;rpm for 1&nbsp;h, and the dark supernatant was the single or few-layered MXene nanosheets suspension.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402178-sec-0150-title"> Preparation of SCMXs and SC Samples</h4>
                  
                  <p>For SCMX6, 100&nbsp;mg of the synthesized MCCHS was added to DI water and sonicated until uniformly dispersed. The MCCHS dispersion (200&nbsp;mL, 0.5&nbsp;mg&nbsp;mL<sup>−1</sup>) was added to a beaker containing 6&nbsp;mg of MXene suspension (0.06&nbsp;mg&nbsp;mL<sup>−1</sup>) and stirred vigorously for 30&nbsp;min. The stirred suspension was vacuum filtered and placed in a vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C for 8&nbsp;h to remove excess water. Finally, the dried precursor and sulfur powder were put into a quartz boat and placed into a tube furnace, which was heated up to 550&nbsp;°C with a heating rate of 2.5&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and held for 2&nbsp;h (Ar atmosphere). After being cooled down to room temperature, the product of the SCMX6 was collected. The SC, SCMX3, and SCMX12 samples followed the same procedure as SCMX6, except that MXene was added at 0, 3, and 12&nbsp;mg, respectively.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402178-sec-0160-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The anode was prepared by blending prepared samples, ketjen black, and carboxymethylcellulose sodium in a mass ratio of 8:1:1 in DI water and then coating it on a Cu foil. In the half-cell test, homemade Na metal was used as a counter/reference electrode, glass fiber (GF/D) was used as the separator, and the 1&nbsp;M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in dimethoxyethane solution as the electrolyte. The mass loading per electrode was ≈0.6–1.0&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. In the full-cell test, the AC cathode was prepared by blending commercial AC powder, carbon nanotubes, and polyvinylidene fluoride in a mass ratio of 8:1:1 in N-methyl-2-pyrrolidone and then coating on a carbon-coated Al foil. And the SCMX6 anode was cycled in half cells for five cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. All coin-type cells (CR2032) are assembled in an Ar-filled glove box (Mikrouna, H<sub>2</sub>O &lt; 0.01&nbsp;ppm, O<sub>2</sub> &lt; 0.01&nbsp;ppm). A Neware battery test system (CT-4008-5V50mA-164, Shenzhen, China) was used to test galvanostatic charge/discharge under different current densities within a potential range of 0.01–3.0&nbsp;V (versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). CV and EIS were tested with an electrochemical workstation (Chenhua CHI660D, Shanghai, China).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402178-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402178-sec-0170-title"> Materials Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The sample morphologies were characterized by SEM (Hitachi S-4800), TEM (JEOL JEM-2100F), and AFM (Bruker Multimode 8 SPM). Physical phases of samples were characterized by XRD (Bruker D8 advance, Cu <i>Kα</i> radiation, λ = 1.5406&nbsp;Å), Raman spectroscopy (Thermo DXR2xi), FT-IR (PerkinElmer Frontier), and Elemental Analysis (UNICUBE Elementar). The surface elemental distribution of the samples was characterized by using XPS (Thermo Scientific ESCALAB Xi+) provided by eceshi (<a href="http://www.eceshi.com" class="linkBehavior">www.eceshi.com</a>). Nitrogen adsorption and desorption (Micromeritics ASAP 2460) were used to characterize the pore size distribution and specific surface area of the samples. Zeta potential (Brookhaven NanoBrook 90Plus PALS) was used to characterize the solid-liquid interfacial electrical properties of the sample dispersion system. Ultraviolet-visible absorbance spectra (Hitachi UH5700) were used to characterize the intensity of MXene absorption peaks.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
